class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Continental League</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Continental_League_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Continental League (disambiguation)">Continental League (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-More_footnotes" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png" width="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article includes a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">list of references</a>, but <b>its sources remain unclear</b> because it has <b>insufficient <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">inline citations</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Fact_and_Reference_Check" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Fact and Reference Check">improve</a> this article by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:When_to_cite" title="Wikipedia:When to cite">introducing</a> more precise citations.</span>  <small><i>(June 2012)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p><p>The <b>Continental League of Professional Baseball Clubs</b> (known as the <b>Continental League</b> or <b>CL</b>) was a proposed third <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">major league</a> for <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> in the United States and Canada, announced in 1959 and scheduled to begin play in the 1961 season. Unlike predecessor competitors such as the <a href="/wiki/Players%27_League" title="Players&#39; League">Players\' League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_League" title="Federal League">Federal League</a>, it sought membership within organized baseball\'s existing organization and acceptance within <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>. The league disbanded in August 1960 without playing a single game as a concession by <a href="/wiki/William_A._Shea" class="mw-redirect" title="William A. Shea">William A. Shea</a> as part of his negotiations with Major League Baseball to expand to incorporate at least eight new teams.\n</p><p>The Continental League was the last serious attempt to create a third major league consisting of new clubs.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Background"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Background</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#New_league_announced"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">New league announced</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Established_leagues_respond"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Established leagues respond</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#The_league_disbands"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">The league disbands</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Legacy"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Legacy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a> (to San Francisco) and the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> (to Los Angeles) moved to <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> following the 1957 season; New York City mayor <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Wagner,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Robert F. Wagner, Jr.">Robert F. Wagner, Jr.</a> appointed a four-man committee to bring the National League back to the city in 1958. Early overtures to entice one of the eight existing NL teams\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> were reportedly approached\xe2\x80\x94were abandoned.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_league_announced">New league announced</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: New league announced">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Continental League was the idea of attorney <a href="/wiki/William_Shea" title="William Shea">William Shea</a>, proposed in November 1958. On July 27, 1959, the new league was formally announced, with teams in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis%E2%80%93St._Paul" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93St. Paul">Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93St. Paul</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The name of the league was said to have been the suggestion of Colorado senator <a href="/wiki/Edwin_C._Johnson" title="Edwin C. Johnson">Edwin C. Johnson</a>.\n</p><p>Representing the team owners at the announcement were <a href="/wiki/Bob_Howsam" title="Bob Howsam">Bob Howsam</a> (Denver), Craig F. Cullinan, Jr. (Houston), <a href="/wiki/Wheelock_Whitney_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wheelock Whitney (politician)">Wheelock Whitney Jr.</a> (Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93St. Paul), Dwight F. Davis, Jr., who was representing the group headed by <a href="/wiki/Joan_Whitney_Payson" title="Joan Whitney Payson">Joan Whitney Payson</a> (New York), and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kent_Cooke" title="Jack Kent Cooke">Jack Kent Cooke</a> (Toronto). Owners in each city had agreed to pay US$50,000 to the league and committed to a capital investment of $2.5 million, not including stadium costs. A minimum <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of 35,000 was established by the league for the venues in which its teams would play.\n</p><p>At least three other teams were expected to be in place before play began in 1961, and the league said it had received applications from 10 cities. The three that were later selected were <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> (announced December 8, 1959),<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_Metroplex" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas\xe2\x80\x93Fort Worth Metroplex">Dallas-Ft. Worth</a> (announced December 22, 1959),<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a> (backed by <a href="/wiki/Robert_O._Swados" title="Robert O. Swados">Robert O. Swados</a> and announced January 29, 1960).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Former Dodgers president <a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a> was named league president on August 18, 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  Appearing in that capacity as a guest on the live <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> broadcast of <i><a href="/wiki/What%27s_My_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="What&#39;s My Line">What\'s My Line</a></i> on Sunday, September 13, 1959, he pronounced the new league as "Inevitable as tomorrow morning."\n</p><p>On February 18, 1960, Rickey and Cooke announced an opening date of April 18, 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Established_leagues_respond">Established leagues respond</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Established leagues respond">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Major League Baseball commissioner\'s office was noncommittal on the issue. At that time, however, the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> enjoyed far more autonomy than they do today, answering more to their constituent owners (who were universally hostile to the new league) than to the Commissioner\'s Office. They reacted to the formation of the new league by announcing plans to expand by adding two teams in each of the existing leagues. Priority would be given, it was stated, to cities that did not have Major League Baseball. Accordingly, the NL placed one of its expansion teams in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> (the then <a href="/wiki/Houston_Colt_.45s" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston Colt .45s">Houston Colt .45s</a>), a Continental League city without an existing Major League Baseball team.\n</p><p>Though the AL placed one of its expansion teams (the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1961%E2%80%9371)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x9371)">Washington Senators</a>) in a previously existing Major League Baseball city (Washington, D.C.), this was done to replace the original Senators team, which had relocated to <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis%E2%80%93St._Paul" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93St. Paul">Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93St. Paul</a> and became the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>. Like Houston, the Twin Cities of Minneapolis/St. Paul were a Continental League city without an existing Major League Baseball team.\n</p><p>The NL then placed another expansion team in New York, offering its tenth franchise to the owners of the Continental League New York team, who immediately accepted, effectively killing any attempt to revive the proposed league. This franchise would become the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>. The AL then followed by placing a second expansion team in Los Angeles, the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">Angels</a>, giving the American League its first presence on the West Coast.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_league_disbands">The league disbands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The league disbands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With Shea\'s mission to bring a second Major League Baseball team to New York successful, he stopped championing the Continental League\'s formation. The promise of expansion achieved the owners\' desired effect; on August 2, 1960, the Continental League formally disbanded.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Although baseball historians concur that Major League Baseball expansion would inevitably have happened due to such factors as pressure from Congress and the rapid growth of professional football, the Continental League undoubtedly forced MLB to hasten expansion by several years. Although Major League Baseball had succeeded in preventing the launch of an eight-team CL, it only did so by committing to eventually adding eight franchises of its own. MLB finished honoring this commitment in 1969 when the AL and NL would each add two more teams for a total of eight over the course of the decade, thereby matching the total number of new teams envisioned by the Continental League.\n</p><p>Although William Shea\'s efforts to create a third major league are not well known today, <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>, home of the New York Mets from 1964 to 2008, was named in his honor for his efforts in bringing National League baseball back to New York.\n</p><p>Of the eight proposed Continental League cities, all but one would eventually receive relocated or expansion Major League Baseball franchises \xe2\x80\x93 Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93St. Paul in 1961, Houston and New York in 1962, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta</a> in 1966, <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Dallas/Ft. Worth</a> in 1972, <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto</a> in 1977, and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Denver</a> in 1993. Buffalo, although it made efforts to lure an MLB team to then-new <a href="/wiki/Sahlen_Field" title="Sahlen Field">Pilot Field</a> in the early 1990s, has not succeeded in bringing Major League Baseball back. (There had been a major league team in Buffalo <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bisons_(NL)" title="Buffalo Bisons (NL)">in the nineteenth century</a>.)  Buffalo remains home to the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bisons" title="Buffalo Bisons">Buffalo Bisons</a>, a team in the <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">Triple-A</a> <a href="/wiki/International_League" title="International League">International League</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://archives.chicagotribune.com/1959/07/28/page/39/article/third-major-baseball-league-formed">"Third Major Baseball League Formed"</a>. <i>The Chicago Tribune</i>. July 28, 1959<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 10,</span> 2017</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Chicago+Tribune&amp;rft.atitle=Third+Major+Baseball+League+Formed&amp;rft.date=1959-07-28&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Farchives.chicagotribune.com%2F1959%2F07%2F28%2Fpage%2F39%2Farticle%2Fthird-major-baseball-league-formed&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AContinental+League"
